# MATERI VOCABULARY — LEVEL B2 (UPPER-INTERMEDIATE)
**Aplikasi:** Inggrisin Yuk | **AI Tutor:** Kak Ara | **Level:** B2 — Upper-Intermediate  
**Total:** 30 Topik Belajar + 1 Placement Test (Day 31)

> **Catatan scope dokumen ini:** Day 1 dan Day 2 sudah lengkap (6 komponen penuh). Day 3–30 menyusul, mengikuti daftar topik dan ATURAN BAKU di bagian bawah dokumen ini agar konsisten.

> **Catatan kebijakan bahasa:** Mulai level ini, bahasa pengantar bergeser jadi **English dominan** (lihat `PRD_USER.md` §5.5 — Kebijakan Bahasa Progressif). Ini bukan keputusan sepihak dokumen ini, tapi konsekuensi langsung dari riset SLA: high-proficiency learners lebih diuntungkan dan lebih memilih English-only environment. Detail penerapannya ada di bagian "Panduan Bahasa untuk Level B2" di bawah.

---

## 🔍 ANALISIS PROMPT KOMPETITOR

### Apa yang Kompetitor Lakukan dengan Baik

Berdasarkan analisis prompt kompetitor (format Kampung Inggris-style ChatGPT prompt) di level Upper-Intermediate:

1. **Box of Words 15 kata** — Tetap dipertahankan di B2, tapi komposisinya melompat jauh: academic/abstract vocabulary, hedging language, dan phrasal verbs idiomatik lanjutan menggantikan kosakata konkret.
2. **Writing Challenge 2 opsi** — Makin krusial karena gap antar-user makin lebar — sebagian sudah lancar conditional/passive, sebagian masih struggle dasar B1.
3. **Koreksi 8 langkah otomatis** — Dipertahankan, tapi langkah Analisa CEFR bergeser fokus ke tips naik ke C1 (Proficient).
4. **Mode Speaking dengan trigger eksplisit** — Makin penting karena speaking di B2 menuntut user mengombinasikan mixed conditional, causative, dan inversion secara real-time saat ngomong — jauh lebih berat dari sekadar 1 grammar per kalimat di B1.
5. **Sistem adaptif berbasis respons** — Dipertahankan, ditingkatkan untuk mendeteksi kapan user siap menerima koreksi yang sepenuhnya dalam English tanpa bantuan Bahasa Indonesia.

### Kelemahan Kompetitor yang Kita Perbaiki

1. **Bahasa pengantar tidak benar-benar bergeser ke English** — Kompetitor sering masih Indonesia-heavy bahkan di level Upper-Intermediate, padahal riset SLA jelas menunjukkan high-proficiency learners justru lebih diuntungkan oleh English-dominant environment. Inggrisin Yuk B2 menerapkan English dominan secara eksplisit dan konsisten (lihat Panduan Bahasa di bawah), bukan sekadar "mix" yang tidak jelas porsinya.
2. **Topik overlap dengan level sebelumnya tidak dipersempit** — Kompetitor sering mengulang topik "Career" atau "Health" yang sama tanpa menaikkan abstraksi. Inggrisin Yuk B2 membatasi overlap ke ~23% (lebih rendah dari B1's 30%) dan mewajibkan setiap overlap membawa grammar B2 yang genuinely baru.
3. **Grammar B2 sering diperkenalkan tanpa kontras eksplisit ke B1** — Kompetitor jarang menjelaskan APA yang berubah dari mixed conditional vs conditional biasa, atau causative vs passive. Inggrisin Yuk B2 selalu kontraskan grammar baru dengan pola B1 yang sudah dikuasai user.
4. **Translation masih dipasang otomatis di semua kalimat** — Bahkan kompetitor yang mengklaim "Upper-Intermediate" masih kasih terjemahan Indonesia di setiap kalimat, yang justru menghambat transisi ke English-only thinking. Inggrisin Yuk B2 hanya kasih catatan Indonesia kalau ada risiko miskonsepsi nyata.
5. **BOW masih terlalu konkret untuk klaim B2** — Kompetitor sering masih pakai kosakata setara B1. Inggrisin Yuk B2 secara sengaja memasukkan academic connectors (notwithstanding, albeit), hedging language (arguably, presumably), dan idiomatic phrasal verbs lanjutan (stem from, account for, delve into).

### Diferensiasi Inggrisin Yuk di Level B2

1. **Bahasa pengantar & koreksi English dominan, dengan "Catatan:" Indonesia HANYA untuk poin berisiko miskonsepsi** — pergeseran kebijakan paling signifikan dibanding semua level sebelumnya, dioperasionalkan secara konkret (lihat tabel BOW 3 kolom & contoh prompt di bawah), bukan sekadar slogan "mix bahasa."
2. **Eskalasi grammar inti B2 di 5 Day pertama** — Mixed Conditionals (Day 1) → Causative Verbs (Day 2) → Inversion for Emphasis (Day 3) → Passive Voice with Modals (Day 4) → Advanced Reported Speech (Day 5). Lima grammar yang paling jelas membedakan B2 dari B1 menurut riset CEFR grammar progression.
3. **Setiap grammar baru dikontraskan eksplisit dengan pola B1** — bukan diperkenalkan dari nol, tapi sebagai "upgrade" dari pola yang sudah user kuasai (contoh: mixed conditional = gabungan 2nd + 3rd conditional yang sudah dipelajari di B1).
4. **BOW mulai memasukkan academic & hedging vocabulary** — trajectory, presumably, notwithstanding, given that — kosakata yang baru relevan begitu user punya cukup grammar kompleks untuk merangkainya.
5. **Topik overlap dengan A1/A2/B1 dibatasi lebih ketat dari B1** — Hanya ~23% (7 dari 30) topik B2 yang menyentuh domain serupa level sebelumnya, dan SETIAP topik overlap WAJIB membawa grammar B2 baru + abstraksi yang genuinely lebih dalam. 77% topik B2 adalah domain yang sama sekali baru (AI, urban planning, justice system, consumer psychology, globalization, dll).

---

## 📊 PERBEDAAN B1 vs B2 — MATERI VOCABULARY

Bagian ini penting untuk diketahui Kak Ara dan tim konten supaya materi B2 tidak sekadar "B1 yang lebih susah" tapi benar-benar mencerminkan perbedaan level CEFR secara pedagogis — termasuk pergeseran kebijakan bahasa yang paling signifikan di seluruh kurikulum.

### Perbedaan Kosakata

| Aspek | B1 (Intermediate) | B2 (Upper-Intermediate) |
|-------|--------------------|--------------------------|
| **Jumlah kata aktif** | ~1.500–2.000 kata aktif (kumulatif A1+A2+B1) | ~3.500–5.000 kata aktif (kumulatif, English Vocabulary Profile/Vocount) |
| **Jenis kata dominan** | Idiomatic phrases, opinion/hedging language dasar, formal-register vocab | + Academic/abstract vocabulary, hedging language lanjutan, phrasal verbs idiomatik kompleks |
| **Contoh kata** | consequence, come up with, as far as I'm concerned, nevertheless | trajectory, stem from, arguably, notwithstanding, conceivably |
| **Morfologi** | Nominalisasi abstrak (-tion, -sion, -ment, -ity) | + Nominalisasi akademik lanjutan (-ism, -ology, -ation kompleks): globalize→globalization, justify→justification |
| **Frasa** | Fixed expressions opini/debat (in my view, on the whole) + phrasal verb idiomatik (come up with, end up) | + Academic connectors (given that, provided that, notwithstanding) + cleft sentence fixed patterns (what really matters is, it's X that) |
| **Register** | Mulai ada formal register berdampingan dengan casual | + Formal register jadi default untuk topik abstrak/profesional, casual tetap dipakai untuk personal/storytelling |

### Perbedaan Grammar yang Diperkenalkan

| Grammar | B1 | B2 |
|---------|----|----|
| Conditional | 2nd Conditional (hipotetis sekarang), 3rd Conditional (penyesalan lampau) — terpisah | + **Mixed Conditionals** (gabungan 2nd+3rd dalam 1 kalimat, time reference berbeda di if-clause vs main clause) |
| Causative | Belum ada | + **Causative verbs** (have/get something done — mendelegasikan tindakan ke orang lain) |
| Emphasis/Inversion | Belum ada | + **Inversion with negative adverbials** (Never have I..., Not only... but also..., Rarely do we...) |
| Voice | Passive di present/past/present perfect simple | + Passive dengan modal (must be done, should have been done) dan passive gerund/infinitive (needs improving, is expected to be finished) |
| Reported Speech | Reported statements & questions + backshift dasar | + **Advanced reporting verbs** (insist on, recommend, deny, suggest) + gerund/that-clause, tanpa selalu backshift jika masih relevan sekarang |
| Modal verbs | Modal of deduction (must be, might be, can't be, must have done) | + Modal of deduction lanjutan dengan nuansa lebih halus (can't have been, should have been able to) |
| Clauses | Defining & non-defining relative clauses | + **Participle clauses** (reduced relative/adverbial: "Tourists wandering without a guide...") + **cleft sentences** (What really matters is...) |
| Lainnya | used to/would, question tags, quantifiers | + Subjunctive formal (It's essential that... be), ellipsis & substitution, verbs of senses + adjective/gerund, "get" multi-makna, hedging language (arguably, to some extent) |

### Perbedaan Struktur Sesi

| Komponen | B1 | B2 |
|----------|----|-----|
| **Mode Cerita** | 5–7 kalimat (bridge Day 22–30: 7–9 kalimat) | 7–9 kalimat (bridge Day 22–30: 9–11 kalimat) |
| **Mode Kilat** | Boleh gabungkan conditional/passive dalam 1 kalimat | Sama, boleh gabungkan mixed conditional/causative/inversion dalam 1 kalimat |
| **Vocab Refresh** | Mulai Day 3 | Mulai **Day 2** — lebih awal lagi karena BOW B2 jauh lebih abstrak (academic/hedging) dan paling cepat lupa tanpa repetisi |
| **Analisa CEFR** | Tips naik ke B2 | Tips naik ke **C1** |
| **Transition Words** | nevertheless, as a result of, in spite of, whereas, on the whole, what's more | + notwithstanding, albeit, given that, provided that, by and large, all things considered |
| **Bahasa koreksi** | Indonesia (utama) + label grammar English lebih sering dipakai | **English dominan.** Indonesia HANYA muncul sebagai "Catatan:" untuk poin berisiko miskonsepsi (interferensi dari Bahasa Indonesia) — lihat Panduan Bahasa B2 |
| **Terjemahan** | Full translation di Speaking Challenge & Paragraf Diperkaya (2 titik scaffolding) | **Tidak ada translation otomatis.** Hanya muncul kalau Kak Ara menilai ada risiko miskonsepsi tinggi |
| **Kompleksitas kalimat** | Maks 16 kata, boleh 2 clause | Maks 20 kata, boleh 2–3 clause (subordinate + relative/conditional + participle) |
| **BOW composition** | Idiomatic phrases, opinion connectors, pasangan register formal/informal | + Academic/abstract nouns, hedging adverbs, phrasal verbs idiomatik lanjutan, academic connectors |

### Mengapa Topik B2 Boleh Overlap dengan A1/A2/B1 (tapi Lebih Terbatas dari B1)

Prinsip **spiral curriculum** tetap berlaku — topik seperti travel, career, education, atau health WAJAR muncul lagi, karena yang berubah adalah **kedalaman abstraksi dan grammar yang dipakai**. Seseorang B1 bisa bilang "If I had known the weather would be bad, I wouldn't have booked that trip" — seseorang B2 bisa bilang "Had I done more research beforehand, I would now be far more prepared for trips like this" (mixed conditional + inversion).

Karena itu, daftar topik B2 di bawah membiarkan **7 dari 30 topik (~23%)** menyentuh domain yang mirip A1/A2/B1 (travel, career, education, health/mental health, job interviews, environment, friendship) — **lebih rendah dari rasio overlap B1 (30%)**, karena:
1. Makin tinggi level, makin banyak domain abstrak/profesional baru yang baru relevan (AI, justice system, globalization, consumer psychology) — semakin sedikit kebutuhan untuk "mengulang" topik lama.
2. User B2 sudah cukup mahir untuk langsung masuk ke domain baru tanpa scaffolding topik familiar — beda dengan B1 yang masih butuh jembatan topik dari A1/A2.

Setiap topik overlap ini WAJIB membawa grammar B2 yang genuinely baru (bukan sekadar mengulang Present Perfect/conditional dasar B1) dan BOW yang lebih abstrak/akademis.

**77% topik B2 (23 dari 30) adalah domain yang sama sekali baru** — artificial intelligence, urban planning, justice system, consumer psychology, globalization, gender roles, risk & decision-making, leadership, digital privacy, economic inequality, immigration — domain yang baru relevan setelah user punya grammar kompleks (mixed conditional, passive modal, subjunctive) untuk membahasnya dengan nuansa.

---

## 📋 DAFTAR 30 TOPIK — LEVEL B2

> **Catatan:** Topik yang ditandai "Overlap" menyentuh domain yang mirip A1/A2/B1, tapi grammar dan BOW-nya didesain genuinely baru — lihat tabel "Perbedaan Grammar" di atas. Topik tanpa tanda adalah domain baru yang belum pernah dibahas di level mana pun sebelumnya.

| Day | Topik | Grammar Utama | Catatan Overlap | Bridge |
|-----|-------|---------------|------------------|--------|
| 1 | Life Choices & Their Lasting Impact | Mixed Conditionals | | |
| 2 | Getting Things Done: Services & Delegation | Causative Verbs (have/get something done) | | |
| 3 | Public Speaking & Memorable Impressions | Inversion with Negative Adverbials | | |
| 4 | Scientific Research & Academic Publishing | Passive Voice with Modals | | |
| 5 | Workplace Conflicts & Negotiation | Advanced Reported Speech (insist, recommend, deny, suggest) | | |
| 6 | Travel Mishaps & Cultural Misunderstandings Abroad | Participle Clauses (reduced relative/adverbial) | Overlap: A1/A2/B1 Travel — kini fokus narasi kompleks dengan reduced clause, bukan info dasar | |
| 7 | Career Pivots & Professional Reinvention | Future Perfect & Future Continuous | Overlap: A2/B1 Career — kini fokus rencana jangka panjang yang presisi waktunya | |
| 8 | Lifelong Learning & Alternative Education Paths | Wish / If Only + Would (complaints) | Overlap: A1/B1 Education — kini fokus kekecewaan & kritik terhadap sistem belajar | |
| 9 | Mental Health & Emotional Wellbeing | Modals of Speculation (Advanced) | Overlap: A1/A2/B1 Health — kini fokus kesehatan mental & deduksi emosional, bukan fisik | |
| 10 | Artificial Intelligence & Its Impact on Daily Life | Future Forms (be about to / be due to / on the verge of) | | |
| 11 | City Life & Urban Planning | Passive Voice with Gerund & Infinitive | | |
| 12 | The Justice System & Fair Trials | Subjunctive in Formal Contexts | | |
| 13 | Marketing Tricks & Consumer Psychology | Cleft Sentences for Emphasis | | |
| 14 | Globalization & Cultural Exchange | Advanced Linking & Discourse Markers | | |
| 15 | Changing Gender Roles in Society | Ellipsis & Substitution | | |
| 16 | Taking Risks: How We Make Big Decisions | Verbs of Senses + Adjective/Gerund | | |
| 17 | Leadership Styles & Team Dynamics | "Get" with Multiple Meanings | | |
| 18 | Digital Privacy & Online Surveillance | Hedging Language (arguably, to some extent) | | |
| 19 | Wealth Gap & Economic Inequality | Academic Connectors (nevertheless, notwithstanding) | | |
| 20 | Salary Negotiation & Advanced Job Interviews | Formal Register + Causative Review | Overlap: A2/B1 Job Interviews — kini fokus negosiasi formal, bukan komunikasi dasar | |
| 21 | Immigration & Multiculturalism | Relative/Participle Clause Review + Hedging | | |
| 22 | Climate Policy & Global Agreements | Mixed Grammar Combo (passive + reported speech + conditional) | Overlap: B1 Environment — kini fokus kebijakan & perjanjian global, bukan sustainability dasar | 🌉 |
| 23 | Maintaining Relationships Across Distance & Time | Future Perfect Continuous + Complex Time Clauses | Overlap: A2/B1 Friendship — kini fokus hubungan jangka panjang lintas waktu/jarak | 🌉 |
| 24 | What Makes a Good Life? Everyday Philosophy | Cleft Sentences + Hedging Combo | | 🌉 |
| 25 | Conspiracy Theories & Critical Thinking | Reported Speech + Modals of Deduction Combo | | 🌉 |
| 26 | Body Language & Nonverbal Communication | Participle Clauses + Verbs of Senses Combo | | 🌉 |
| 27 | Generational Differences (Gen Z vs Boomers) | Comparatives Advanced + Inversion Review | | 🌉 |
| 28 | The Future of Work & Automation | Future Forms Combo (future perfect + continuous + be about to) | | 🌉 |
| 29 | Free Speech & Censorship Debates | Subjunctive + Cleft Sentence Combo | | 🌉 |
| 30 | Narrative Mastery (All B2 Grammar Combined) | Semua grammar B2 dikombinasikan | | 🌉 |
| 31 | Placement Test B2 → C1 | Semua grammar B2 | | |

> 🌉 **Day 22–30** adalah zona Bridge B2→C1: grammar dan kosakata mulai menyentuh area C1 (nuansa register, cohesion tingkat paragraf, idiomatic precision) secara controlled. User tetap dinilai di level B2 tapi diperkenalkan pola C1 secara bertahap.

---

## 📐 STRUKTUR MATERI PER SESI

### Komponen Setiap Day

Setiap sesi belajar Vocabulary B2 terdiri dari 6 komponen yang berjalan secara berurutan — identik dengan A1/A2/B1 dalam struktur, berbeda signifikan dalam bahasa pengantar dan tuntutan konten:

**1. Detail Materi**
Setiap day memiliki 1 topik spesifik. BOW 15 kata dikurasi dengan komposisi yang sudah bergeser dari B1: academic/abstract vocabulary, hedging language, dan phrasal verbs idiomatik lanjutan. Semua kata disertai phonetic symbol UK dan **definisi singkat dalam English** — bukan lagi arti Bahasa Indonesia secara default (lihat Panduan Bahasa B2). Grammar Pendukung mencakup pola-pola B2 (mixed conditional, causative, inversion, passive modal, dll), dijelaskan dalam English dengan kontras eksplisit ke pola B1 yang relevan.

**2. Detail Task**
User diberikan 2 mode Writing Challenge, instruksi dalam English:
- 📖 Mode Cerita: Write **7–9 sentences** (naik dari B1's 5–7) tentang konteks topik, gunakan minimal 5 kata dari BOW.
- ⚡ Mode Kilat: Pilih 5 kata dari BOW, buat 1 kalimat untuk setiap kata (boleh gunakan grammar B2 seperti mixed conditional/causative dalam 1 kalimat).

**3. Detail Review & Koreksi (8 Langkah)**
Setelah user mengirim tulisan, AI langsung menjalankan koreksi 8 langkah:
1. Koreksi Writing — tabel kalimat asli vs benar, plus "Kenapa" dalam English (Catatan Indonesia HANYA untuk 1-2 pola error yang murni disebabkan interferensi Bahasa Indonesia).
2. Analisa BOW — cek ketepatan penggunaan. Mulai Day 2: + 🔂 Vocab Refresh.
3. Analisa CEFR — penilaian level saat ini dan **tips naik ke C1**.
4. Perbandingan 5W+1H — perkaya tulisan dengan elemen Who/What/Where/When/Why/How, dalam English, tanpa translation default.
5. Transition Words — rekomendasi academic connectors level B2 (notwithstanding, albeit, given that, by and large).
6. Lexical Chunks & Collocation Check — 2–3 natural collocations atau fixed expressions yang dipakai native B2+ untuk topik ini.
7. Register/Formality Check — cek konsistensi register (terlalu kasual/kaku untuk konteks topik). ✅ jika sudah konsisten.
8. Speaking Challenge — 3 pertanyaan speaking dalam English (tanpa translation default); minimal 1 memicu retrieval dari pola yang baru dikoreksi.

**4. Detail Feedback**
Feedback dalam **English**, encouraging, dengan tone upper-intermediate native-like. Catatan Indonesia HANYA muncul kalau ada poin yang berisiko bikin user salah paham karena perbedaan struktural dengan Bahasa Indonesia.

**5. Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)**
Trigger: mode suara ChatGPT 🎙️ + "Let's start speaking!". 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, dalam English. Sistem adaptif: lancar → 1 pertanyaan lanjutan; macet → contoh kalimat + pattern drill (feedback tetap English, clue tambahan boleh pakai Bahasa Indonesia singkat kalau user benar-benar stuck).

**6. PROMPT siap pakai**
Setiap topik dilengkapi prompt siap copy-paste ke ChatGPT, dengan [TOPIC] dan [TOPIC_CONTEXT] sudah terisi nilai asli.

---

### Alur Sesi (User Flow)

```
User klik topik di dashboard (misal: Day 1 — Life Choices & Their Lasting Impact)
         ↓
Halaman detail topik terbuka — tampil deskripsi singkat + tombol "Mulai Belajar"
         ↓
User klik "Mulai Belajar" → ChatGPT terbuka dengan prompt sudah terisi
         ↓
Kak Ara menyapa (English dominan) + langsung tampilkan BOX OF WORDS (tabel 15 kata)
         ↓
Kak Ara tampilkan WRITING CHALLENGE (Mode Cerita & Mode Kilat) dalam 1 response
         ↓
User memilih Mode Cerita atau Mode Kilat → mengetik dan mengirim jawaban tulisannya
         ↓
Kak Ara langsung menjalankan KOREKSI 8 LANGKAH secara otomatis
(Koreksi Writing + Kenapa → Analisa BOW (+ Vocab Refresh sejak Day 2) → Analisa CEFR → 5W+1H → Transition Words → Lexical Chunks & Collocation Check → Register/Formality Check → Speaking Challenge sebagai retrieval practice)
         ↓
User membaca feedback (English) → siap lanjut ke speaking
         ↓
User aktifkan mode suara ChatGPT 🎙️, lalu bilang: "Let's start speaking!"
         ↓
Kak Ara mengajukan pertanyaan Speaking Challenge SATU PER SATU
         ↓
User menjawab setiap pertanyaan → Kak Ara beri feedback + koreksi per jawaban
         ↓
Selesai → Kak Ara beri pujian singkat di akhir sesi
         ↓
User kembali ke app → topik otomatis tertandai ✓ (progress +1)
```

---

### Panduan Bahasa untuk Level B2

> Ini adalah pergeseran kebijakan paling signifikan di seluruh kurikulum Inggrisin Yuk — lihat `PRD_USER.md` §5.5 untuk dasar risetnya.

| Aspek | Detail |
|-------|--------|
| **Bahasa pengantar & penjelasan** | **English dominan.** Grammar Pendukung, konteks penggunaan, semua dijelaskan dalam English |
| **Bahasa koreksi** | English dominan. "Catatan:" Bahasa Indonesia HANYA muncul untuk poin yang berisiko miskonsepsi karena interferensi struktur Bahasa Indonesia (maks 1-2 per Day) |
| **Terjemahan** | **Tidak otomatis.** BOW pakai definisi singkat English, bukan arti Indonesia. Speaking Challenge & Paragraf Diperkaya TIDAK pakai translation default lagi (beda dari B1) |
| **Kompleksitas kalimat** | S+V+O+extension, maksimal 20 kata, boleh 2–3 clause (subordinate + relative/conditional + participle) |
| **Grammar yang diperkenalkan** | Mixed Conditionals, Causative Verbs, Inversion, Passive (modal & gerund/infinitive), Advanced Reported Speech, Subjunctive, Cleft Sentences, Participle Clauses, Hedging Language |
| **Vocabulary density** | 15 kata per sesi: academic/abstract nouns, hedging adverbs, phrasal verbs idiomatik lanjutan, academic connectors |
| **Feedback style** | Encouraging, tone native-like upper-intermediate. Tidak childish, tidak terlalu formal/textbook |
| **Kalau user benar-benar stuck** | Boleh kasih 1 clue singkat Bahasa Indonesia (bukan kalimat penuh) — fallback scaffolding, bukan default |

---

### Panduan Pemilihan 15 BOW per Topik (B2)

| Kategori | Jumlah | Kriteria Pemilihan |
|----------|--------|---------------------|
| **Nouns (kata benda)** | 4–5 kata | Mayoritas academic/abstract nouns (trajectory, outcome, circumstance) — bukan lagi sekadar abstract nouns biasa seperti di B1. |
| **Verbs (kata kerja)** | 4–5 kata | Termasuk 1–2 phrasal verb idiomatik lanjutan per Day (stem from, account for, delve into, get around to). Bentuk V3 penting untuk passive modal dicantumkan di Grammar Pendukung. |
| **Adjectives / Adverbs** | 3–4 kata | Termasuk hedging adverbs (presumably, arguably, conceivably) dan adjective bernuansa (pivotal, irreversible, plausible). |
| **Fixed expressions / Academic connectors** | 1–2 frasa | given that, provided that, in retrospect, by and large — diprioritaskan yang relevan dengan topik. |

**Prinsip utama pemilihan BOW B2:**
- Academic-first — di B2 user sudah siap untuk "trajectory", "circumstance", "outcome" sejak Day 1, bukan lagi kosakata konkret.
- Setiap Day yang memuat Passive Modal/Causative WAJIB menyertakan minimal 1 contoh V3 form di Grammar Pendukung.
- Phrasal verb idiomatik lanjutan (stem from, account for, delve into) diprioritaskan satu per Day.
- Hedging language dipilih yang benar-benar dipakai native speaker dalam diskusi formal/semi-formal, bukan textbook-only phrases.
- Definisi BOW default dalam English sederhana; Catatan Indonesia HANYA kalau kata tersebut benar-benar berisiko disalahpahami (false friend, idiom yang tidak punya analogi langsung di Bahasa Indonesia).

---

## 🎯 PROMPT TEMPLATE INGGRISIN YUK — VOCABULARY B2

### Cara Pakai

| Variabel | Cara Isi | Contoh |
|----------|----------|--------|
| `[PANGGILAN]` | Sapaan dari profil di aplikasi — default `Kak`, bisa diubah di Edit Profil | `Kak` |
| `[NAMA]` | Nama panggilan user dari profil di aplikasi | `Dhafran` |
| `[TOPIC]` | Nama topik hari ini sesuai daftar 30 topik | `Life Choices & Their Lasting Impact` |
| `[TOPIC_CONTEXT]` | Konteks writing challenge yang spesifik untuk topik ini | `keputusan masa lalu yang masih memengaruhi hidupmu sampai sekarang` |

---

### Prompt Template Dasar

```
Topik: [TOPIC]
Panggil aku [PANGGILAN] [NAMA].
Level bahasa Inggrisku: B2 (Upper-Intermediate).
Kamu Kak Ara, personal AI Coach kamu, dari Inggrisin Yuk. Tugasmu membimbingku belajar vocab lewat writing dan speaking di Level B2 (Upper-Intermediate).

Gaya bahasa: sopan, ramah, casual, friendly, dan humble (rendah hati — tidak menggurui, hargai usaha user) — tunjukkan lewat caramu ngobrol, jangan deskripsi diri sendiri dengan kata-kata seperti "seru" atau "asyik".
Gunakan English sebagai bahasa utama untuk penjelasan, instruksi, dan koreksi. Bahasa Indonesia HANYA untuk catatan singkat ("Catatan:") di poin yang berisiko bikin aku salah paham karena beda struktur dengan Bahasa Indonesia — maksimal 1-2 catatan per sesi, bukan default.
Pakai emoji secukupnya biar enak dibaca.
Tampilkan phonetic symbol UK setelah setiap kosakata dalam tanda / /. Kata pendek di samping vocab, frasa panjang di baris bawah.

---

LANGKAH 1 — GREETING + BOX OF WORDS + WRITING CHALLENGE (dalam 1 response):

Sapa santai dalam English: "Hi! It's Kak Ara from Inggrisin Yuk 👋", lalu langsung tampilkan Box of Words dan Writing Challenge. Jangan tanya "ready?" atau "shall we continue?" — langsung kasih challenge-nya.

📦 Box of Words:
Buatkan 15 kosakata yang pas untuk topik [TOPIC] di level B2. Kombinasikan: verbs (termasuk 1–2 phrasal verb idiomatik lanjutan), nouns (mayoritas academic/abstract), adjectives/adverbs (boleh hedging language), dan 1–2 academic connector/fixed expression. Pilih kata yang frekuensi tinggi dan natural dipakai native speaker di konteks semi-formal.

Tampilkan dalam tabel bernomor 3 kolom:
- Kolom 1: Kosakata + phonetic symbol UK
- Kolom 2: Definisi singkat dalam English (simple, B2-level)
- Kolom 3: Catatan Indonesia — isi "–" kecuali kata tersebut benar-benar berisiko disalahpahami
Jangan tambah kolom lain.

✍️ Writing Challenge (tampilkan 2 mode sekaligus):
📖 Mode Cerita: Write 7–9 sentences tentang [TOPIC_CONTEXT]. Pakai minimal 5 kata dari Box of Words.
⚡ Mode Kilat: Pilih 5 kata dari Box of Words, buat 1 kalimat untuk setiap kata.

Format tampilan setiap mode:
(a) 1 kalimat deskripsi singkat di bawah nama mode — apa yang membedakannya.
(b) 1 contoh singkat (bukan jawaban lengkap) — WAJIB gunakan KATA YANG SAMA dari Box of Words untuk kedua mode.
(c) Template Latihan:
- Mode Cerita → baris bernomor kosong (1. ... 2. ... dst) untuk aku isi sendiri.
- Mode Kilat → format "kata: ..." pakai 5 kata pilihanmu dari Box of Words.

Jangan bocorkan langkah koreksi — fokus ke challenge dulu, tunggu jawabanku.

---

LANGKAH 2 — KOREKSI 8 LANGKAH (otomatis setelah aku kirim tulisan):

1️⃣ Koreksi Writing
Tabel 3 kolom: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (penjelasan dalam English). Tambahkan "Catatan:" Bahasa Indonesia HANYA untuk maksimal 1-2 pola error yang murni disebabkan interferensi Bahasa Indonesia — sisanya cukup penjelasan English.
Kalimat yang sudah ≥95% benar: tandai ✅ di kolom Kalimat Asli, kolom Why isi "—".

2️⃣ Analisa Box of Words
Cek setiap kata BOW yang aku pakai: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat, dengan contoh kalimat natural dalam English.
[Mulai Day 2] Tambahkan 🔂 Vocab Refresh: singgung balik 1–2 kata dari BOW Day sebelumnya.

3️⃣ Analisa CEFR
Nilai tulisanku dalam English: level saat ini, apa yang sudah bagus, dan 1–2 tips konkret buat naik ke C1.
Gunakan bahasa yang encouraging, bukan judging.

4️⃣ Perbandingan 5W+1H
Tabel 2 kolom dalam English: elemen 5W+1H dari tulisanku vs versi yang lebih lengkap.
Di bawah tabel, "Enriched Paragraph": versi tulisanku yang diperkaya, full English, TANPA translation Indonesia (beda dari B1).

5️⃣ Transition Words
Cek apakah aku sudah pakai academic connector. Jika belum, rekomendasikan 2–3 dari: notwithstanding, albeit, given that, provided that, by and large, all things considered.
Format: connector + contoh kalimat singkat dalam English.

6️⃣ Lexical Chunks & Collocation Check
Give 2–3 natural collocations or fixed expressions native B2+ speakers reach for on the topic of [TOPIC] — multi-word units, not individual words. Format: chunk in bold + one-line usage note (English). Check whether my writing used natural collocations or read as word-for-word translation from Indonesian. Suggest 1 chunk to incorporate if none detected.
If my writing is blank, off-topic, or entirely in Indonesian: politely ask me to write 7–9 English sentences first, before running Step 2.

7️⃣ Register/Formality Check
Identify 1-2 phrases where the register doesn't match the topic's context (too casual for formal topics, or overly academic for conversational ones). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (English, 1 sentence). ✅ skip if register is consistent throughout.
If my writing is blank, off-topic, or entirely in Indonesian: politely ask me to write 7–9 English sentences first, before running Step 2.

8️⃣ Speaking Challenge
Beri 3 pertanyaan speaking dalam English berdasarkan topik [TOPIC], TANPA translation Indonesia default.
WAJIB: minimal 1 dari 3 pertanyaan dirancang supaya aku terpaksa pakai ulang pola yang baru dikoreksi di Langkah 1.

---

LANGKAH 3 — MODE SPEAKING (trigger: user aktifkan mode suara ChatGPT 🎙️ lalu bilang "Let's start speaking!"):

- Ulangi 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu — jangan semua sekaligus, dalam English
- Transkrip jawabanku dalam Bahasa Inggris walau aku campur bahasa
- Semua koreksi dan respons dalam English. Kalau aku benar-benar stuck, boleh kasih 1 clue singkat Bahasa Indonesia

Feedback setelah setiap jawaban:
• Versi kalimat yang lebih baik (level B2) + penjelasan singkat dalam English kenapa lebih baik
• Kalau ada error grammar B2 (mixed conditional, causative, inversion), tulis bentuk yang benar dalam kurung italic.

Kalau aku bilang "clue": kasih petunjuk grammar saja dalam English (atau Bahasa Indonesia singkat kalau aku benar-benar stuck), bukan jawaban penuh.
Kalau lancar → tambah 1 pertanyaan lanjutan yang lebih detail.
Kalau macet → beri 1 contoh kalimat pendek, latih dengan pattern drill, ulangi pertanyaannya.

Prioritas koreksi: (1) makna, (2) urutan kata, (3) bentuk grammar B2 (mixed conditional, causative, inversion, passive modal), (4) articles/preposisi.
Pujian singkat hanya di akhir sesi — tulus, tidak berlebihan.
```

## 📋 ATURAN BAKU — WAJIB DIIKUTI UNTUK DAY 1–30 + PLACEMENT TEST (DAY 31)

Bagian ini adalah rujukan tunggal (*single source of truth*) supaya Day 3–30 dan Day 31 Placement Test yang akan dibuat nanti tetap 100% konsisten dengan Day 1–2 yang sudah jadi. **Baca bagian ini dulu sebelum menulis materi Day baru.**

### A. Persona & Bahasa (tidak boleh berubah di Day mana pun)

| Aspek | Aturan |
|-------|--------|
| Nama AI | **Kak Ara** — personal AI Coach kamu, dari Inggrisin Yuk. Tunjukkan personality lewat gaya bicara, jangan deskripsikan diri sendiri dengan kata seperti "seru"/"asyik" |
| Sapaan ke user | `[PANGGILAN] [NAMA]` — selalu PANGGILAN dulu baru NAMA. Default = `Kak`. Auto-fill dari profil user |
| Bahasa pengantar & koreksi | **English dominan.** "Catatan:" Bahasa Indonesia HANYA untuk poin berisiko miskonsepsi karena interferensi struktur Bahasa Indonesia, maksimal 1-2 per Day. Tidak ada translation otomatis lagi (beda dari A1/A2/B1) |
| Phonetic | UK English, format `/ /`, ditempel di samping kata pendek atau baris bawah untuk frasa panjang |

### B. Trigger & Mekanisme Respons

| Trigger | Aturan |
|---------|--------|
| Mulai sesi (Langkah 1) | BOW + Writing Challenge tampil dalam **1 response**, tanpa nanya "ready?" atau "shall we continue?" |
| Speaking Mode (Langkah 3) | Diaktifkan HANYA lewat ucapan suara 🎙️: **"Let's start speaking!"** |
| Minta petunjuk saat speaking | User bilang **"clue"** → AI kasih petunjuk grammar (English, atau Bahasa Indonesia singkat kalau user stuck) |
| Urutan pertanyaan speaking | Satu per satu. Lancar → +1 pertanyaan lanjutan. Macet → contoh kalimat pendek + pattern drill |
| Prioritas koreksi speaking | (1) makna → (2) urutan kata → (3) bentuk grammar B2 (mixed conditional, causative, inversion, passive modal) → (4) articles/preposisi |

### C. Box of Words — 15 kata per Day

| Kategori | Jumlah | Catatan |
|----------|--------|---------|
| Nouns | 4–5 | Mayoritas academic/abstract (trajectory, outcome, circumstance) |
| Verbs | 4–5 | 1–2 phrasal verb idiomatik lanjutan per Day OK (stem from, account for, delve into, get around to) |
| Adjectives / Adverbs | 3–4 | Boleh hedging adverb (presumably, arguably, conceivably) dan adjective bernuansa (pivotal, irreversible, plausible) |
| Fixed expressions / Academic connectors | 1–2 | given that, provided that, in retrospect, by and large — relevan dengan topik |

Tabel BOW WAJIB 3 kolom: Kosakata+phonetic | Definisi singkat English | Catatan Indonesia ("–" default, isi hanya jika berisiko miskonsepsi).

**🔂 Vocab Refresh (WAJIB mulai Day 2):** Langkah 2 harus singgung balik 1–2 kata dari BOW Day N-1 (lebih awal dari B1 karena BOW B2 lebih abstrak dan paling cepat lupa). Di Day 6–9, boleh sesekali singgung kosakata B1 Bridge (Day 22–30 B1) untuk kontinuitas lintas level.

### D. Writing Challenge — 2 Mode

- 📖 **Mode Cerita** — kalimat-kalimat **terhubung** seperti bercerita (**7–9 kalimat**). Bridge Day 22–30: **9–11 kalimat**.
- ⚡ **Mode Kilat** — latih kata secara **terpisah** (1 kalimat per kata). Boleh pakai grammar B2 (mixed conditional/causative/inversion) dalam kalimat.
- **WAJIB untuk KEDUA mode:** (a) 1 kalimat deskripsi singkat di bawah nama mode (b) 1 CONTOH singkat — **KATA YANG SAMA** dari BOW untuk kedua mode (c) TEMPLATE LATIHAN.
- Instruksi task dalam English (beda dari B1 yang masih Indonesia).

### E. Koreksi 8 Langkah — metodologi

| # | Langkah | Aturan Konten |
|---|---------|---------------|
| 1️⃣ | Koreksi Writing | Tabel: Kalimat Asli → Kalimat Benar → **Why** (English). "Catatan:" Indonesia HANYA untuk maks 1-2 pola error berbasis interferensi Bahasa Indonesia. ✅ untuk kalimat ≥95% benar |
| 2️⃣ | Analisa BOW | ✅/⚠️ per kata + contoh natural English. **Mulai Day 2:** + 🔂 Vocab Refresh |
| 3️⃣ | Analisa CEFR | Level saat ini + **1–2 tips konkret naik ke C1**. Bahasa encouraging, dalam English |
| 4️⃣ | Perbandingan 5W+1H | Tabel What/Why/Where/When/Who/How (English). Di bawahnya "Enriched Paragraph" — full English, TANPA translation default |
| 5️⃣ | Transition Words | Rekomendasikan 2–3 dari: notwithstanding, albeit, given that, provided that, by and large, all things considered + contoh English |
| 6️⃣ | Lexical Chunks & Collocation Check | 2–3 natural collocations or fixed expressions native B2+ speakers reach for in this context. Format: chunk + one-line usage note (English). Check whether the user's writing used natural collocations, or read as word-for-word translation from Indonesian. Suggest 1 chunk to incorporate if none detected. |
| 7️⃣ | Register/Formality Check | Identify 1-2 phrases where the register doesn't match the topic's context (too casual for formal, or overly academic for conversational). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (English, 1 sentence). ✅ skip if consistent throughout. |
| 8️⃣ | Speaking Challenge | 3 pertanyaan dalam English, tanpa translation default. **WAJIB:** min 1 memicu retrieval dari pola yang baru dikoreksi di Langkah 1 |

**Research basis for Step 6:** *Lexical Approach* (Lewis, 1993) — fluency is driven more by mastery of *lexical chunks* (multi-word units learned as wholes) than by constructing sentences word by word. At B2, the gap between grammatically correct and natively natural writing is largely a collocation gap — Step 6 addresses this directly.

### F. Skeleton Dokumen — wajib 6 sub-bagian per Day, urutan tetap

1. `#### 📚 Detail Materi` — tabel BOW (3 kolom) + Grammar Pendukung (B2) + Konteks Penggunaan
2. `#### ✅ Detail Task` — Mode Cerita + Mode Kilat (dengan contoh) + Speaking Challenge (3 pertanyaan, English)
3. `#### 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi (8 Langkah)` — error & pola spesifik topik
4. `#### 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara` — tone guide, error umum, template pujian, tips naik level
5. `#### 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)` — skenario, pertanyaan lanjutan, pattern drill
6. `#### 🔗 PROMPT — Day N (Copy-Paste ke ChatGPT)` — prompt lengkap siap pakai

### G. Penomoran Day & Daftar Topik

Day 1–30 = 1 topik per hari, Day 31 = Placement Test B2→C1. Master daftar topik ada di tabel "DAFTAR 30 TOPIK" di atas.

Logika urutan: Day 1–5 grammar utama B2 (Mixed Conditionals → Causative → Inversion → Passive Modal → Advanced Reported Speech) → Day 6–9 topik overlap A1/A2/B1 dengan grammar lebih dalam → Day 10–14 domain abstrak baru (AI, urban planning, justice, consumer psychology, globalization) → Day 15–17 ellipsis, verbs of senses, "get" multi-makna → Day 18–21 hedging, academic connectors, formal register, immigration → Day 22–30 🌉 Bridge ke C1 → Day 31 Placement Test.

### H. Placement Test (Day 31) — format baku

| Komponen | Detail |
|----------|--------|
| Jumlah soal | 20–25 soal per sesi |
| Format | Pilih kata yang tepat / lengkapi kalimat / identifikasi kesalahan / mini production — instruksi dalam English |
| Fokus | Kosakata Day 1–30 B2 + grammar B2 (mixed conditional, causative, inversion, passive modal, subjunctive) |
| Output | Score + rekomendasi: lanjut ke C1 / review topik tertentu / ulangi Day tertentu — dalam English |
| Bisa diulang | Ya, kapan saja |

## 📚 MATERI 30 TOPIK + PLACEMENT TEST

---

### DAY 1 — Life Choices & Their Lasting Impact

#### 📚 Detail Materi

**Target Kosakata (Box of Words):**

| No | Kosakata + Phonetic UK | English Definition | Catatan Indonesia |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | trajectory /trəˈdʒektəri/ | the general direction in which something develops over time | – |
| 2 | outcome /ˈaʊtkʌm/ | the final result of an action or situation | – |
| 3 | pivotal /ˈpɪvətl/ | extremely important because it influences later events | – |
| 4 | irreversible /ˌɪrɪˈvɜːsəbl/ | impossible to change back to a previous state | – |
| 5 | hindsight /ˈhaɪndsaɪt/ | understanding of a situation only after it has happened | Bahasa Indonesia tidak punya 1 kata untuk ini — sering diterjemahkan "menyesal" padahal artinya lebih ke "baru sadar setelah lewat", bukan penyesalan itu sendiri |
| 6 | foresight /ˈfɔːsaɪt/ | the ability to predict what will happen and plan accordingly | – |
| 7 | presumably /prɪˈzjuːməbli/ | used to say that something is likely true, based on what you know | – |
| 8 | inevitably /ɪnˈevɪtəbli/ | in a way that cannot be avoided | – |
| 9 | stem from (phrasal verb) /stem frɒm/ | to be caused by or originate from something | – |
| 10 | account for (phrasal verb) /əˈkaʊnt fɔːr/ | to explain the reason for something | – |
| 11 | in retrospect /ɪn ˈretrəspekt/ | when looking back at a past event, with current knowledge | – |
| 12 | given that (fixed expression) /ˈɡɪvən ðæt/ | considering the fact that | – |
| 13 | circumstance /ˈsɜːkəmstəns/ | a fact or condition connected with an event | – |
| 14 | reflect on (phrasal verb) /rɪˈflekt ɒn/ | to think carefully about something, often a past experience | – |
| 15 | shape (verb, abstract use) /ʃeɪp/ | to strongly influence the form or nature of something | Hati-hati: ini BUKAN "shape" sebagai kata benda (bentuk) — di sini verb, artinya "membentuk" secara abstrak, misalnya membentuk karakter atau masa depan |

**Grammar Pendukung (B2):**
- **Mixed Conditional — Past Condition → Present Result** (past condition → present result): **Past Perfect** in the if-clause + **would** + V1 in the main clause → "If I **had studied** medicine, I **would be** a doctor now." The condition is about the past, but the result is still true today.
- **Mixed Conditional — Present Condition → Past Result** (present/general condition → past result): **Past Simple** in the if-clause + **would have** + V3 in the main clause → "If I **were** braver, I **would have taken** that job." The condition describes a general truth about the person, but the result happened in the past.
- **Contrast with B1:** In B1, 2nd and 3rd conditionals always match their time reference in both clauses (2nd = present/present, 3rd = past/past). In B2, mixed conditionals deliberately combine **two different time references** in one sentence — this is what makes them sound more natural and "native-like" when talking about real, complex life situations.
- **Quick test:** ask yourself "Is the if-clause about the past, and the result about now?" → Past Condition → Present Result. "Is the if-clause about a general truth, and the result about the past?" → Present Condition → Past Result.

**Konteks Penggunaan:**
These words and structures are used to reflect on past decisions and how they continue to shape the present — or to imagine how a different past would have led to a different present. Mixed conditionals are one of the clearest markers of B2: at B1, a learner can only express a hypothetical situation as a "clean" if-then pair with matching time references. At B2, a learner can connect a hypothetical *past* to a hypothetical *present* in a single sentence — which is exactly how people naturally reflect on life choices.

---

#### ✅ Detail Task

**📖 Mode Cerita:**
Connected sentences that build one reflection on a life decision and its lasting effect.
Example (using "trajectory"): "My career trajectory changed completely after I took that internship. If I hadn't taken it, I would probably be in a completely different field now."
Write 7–9 sentences about a decision you made in the past that still affects your life today — it could be about education, a relationship, a job, or a move to a new city. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words.
1. ...
2. ...
3. ...
4. ...
5. ...
6. ...
7. ...
(add sentence 8 and 9 if you want)

**⚡ Mode Kilat:**
Practice each word separately — 1 sentence per word, not connected as a story.
Example (same word "trajectory"): "trajectory: If I had chosen a different university, my career trajectory would look completely different today."
Choose 5 words from the Box of Words and write 1 mixed conditional sentence for each:
- hindsight: ...
- pivotal: ...
- stem from: ...
- in retrospect: ...
- shape: ...

**Speaking Challenge (3 Pertanyaan):**
1. **Looking back, is there a pivotal decision that, in hindsight, you would have made differently?**
2. **If you had grown up in a different city or country, how do you think your life would be different now?**
3. **What circumstance from your past do you think has shaped who you are today, even if you didn't realize it at the time?**

---

#### 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi (8 Langkah)

**Langkah 1 — Koreksi Writing:**
Common errors among Indonesian learners with Mixed Conditionals (top 2 patterns get a deep "Why" explanation):
1. Matching tenses incorrectly across clauses: "If I studied medicine, I would be a doctor now" (missing the past condition) → "If I **had studied** medicine, I **would be** a doctor now." — *Why: this is a Past-Condition → Present-Result mixed conditional — the condition happened in the past (or didn't happen), but the result is about NOW. Many learners default to a "clean" 2nd conditional pattern (Past Simple + would) because that's what they learned in B1 — but here the condition itself needs to be in the past (Past Perfect), since we're talking about a decision that was or wasn't made years ago. Catatan: Bahasa Indonesia tidak membedakan "kalau saya belajar" (sekarang) dari "kalau saya sudah belajar (dulu)" dengan jelas — keduanya bisa terasa sama, padahal di English ini menentukan apakah pakai Past Simple atau Past Perfect di if-clause.*
2. Using "would" instead of "would have" when the result is about the past: "If I were braver, I would take that job" (when referring to a past missed opportunity) → "If I **were** braver, I **would have taken** that job." — *Why: this is a Present-Condition → Past-Result mixed conditional — the condition is a general truth about you (still true now), but the result refers to a specific moment in the past that you missed. "Would have + V3" signals that the result already happened (or didn't happen) in the past, even though the condition is still ongoing.*
3. Forgetting Past Perfect in the if-clause: "If I have known earlier, I would be more prepared" → "If I **had known** earlier, I would be more prepared." — have/has is Present Perfect, not Past Perfect; mixed conditionals need **had** + V3 in the if-clause for the Past-Condition → Present-Result pattern.

**Langkah 2 — Analisa BOW:**
Words that are often misused:
- **hindsight** vs **foresight**: opposites — "hindsight" = looking back with clarity ("In **hindsight**, I should have saved more money"), "foresight" = predicting ahead of time ("She had the **foresight** to invest early"). Don't confuse the direction.
- **stem from**: always followed by a noun or gerund, never a full clause directly — "This problem **stems from** a lack of communication." (✅) not "stems that..." (❌).
- **account for**: has two different meanings depending on context — "explain" ("Can you **account for** the missing data?") or "make up a proportion of" ("Tourism **accounts for** 30% of the country's income"). Context decides which meaning applies.
- **given that**: always followed by a clause (subject + verb), functions like "considering that" — "**Given that** I had no experience, the interview went surprisingly well."

**Langkah 3 — Analisa CEFR:**
Template: "Your writing is solid for B2! The mixed conditional structure is coming through naturally — that's a real upgrade from B1's matched-tense conditionals. To move toward C1, try: (1) combining a mixed conditional with inversion for extra emphasis ('Had I known then what I know now, I would be in a very different place'), (2) varying your hedging language instead of relying on simple statements — 'arguably', 'in all likelihood', 'conceivably' add nuance that native speakers use naturally."

**Langkah 4 — 5W+1H:**
Example table for the topic Life Choices:
| Elemen | Versi User | Versi Lebih Lengkap |
|---|---|---|
| What | I changed my career path | I made a pivotal decision to change my career path entirely |
| When | a few years ago | back in my early twenties, right after finishing university |
| Where | (not mentioned) | while I was still living in my hometown |
| Why | (not mentioned) | because I realized the trajectory I was on no longer matched my values |
| Who | I | I, with some encouragement from a mentor |
| How | (not mentioned) | by taking a significant financial risk that, in hindsight, paid off |

**Enriched Paragraph:**
"Looking back, the decision to change my career path was pivotal. If I hadn't taken that risk back then, I would probably still be stuck in a job that no longer matched my values. In retrospect, it's clear that this single choice shaped the trajectory of everything that followed."

**Langkah 5 — Transition Words:**
Best-fitting connectors for discussing life choices and their impact (B2 level):
- **given that** → "Given that I had no formal training, the outcome was better than expected."
- **in retrospect** → "In retrospect, that decision was the turning point of my whole career."
- **all things considered** → "All things considered, I don't regret taking that risk."

**Langkah 6 — Lexical Chunks & Collocation Check:**
Natural collocations B2+ speakers use for Life Choices: "shape one's identity", "turn one's life around", "look back on a decision", "make a pivotal choice". Cek apakah tulisan user menggunakan collocation natural atau terdengar seperti terjemahan kata-per-kata dari Bahasa Indonesia. Sarankan 1 chunk kalau belum muncul.

**Langkah 7 — Register/Formality Check:**
Identify 1-2 phrases where the register doesn't match the topic's context (too casual for a reflective/formal topic, or overly academic/stiff for personal storytelling). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (English, 1 sentence). ✅ skip if register is consistent throughout.

**Langkah 8 — Speaking Challenge:**
Question #1 ("is there a pivotal decision that, in hindsight, you would have made differently?") directly triggers a Present-Condition → Past-Result mixed conditional — the same pattern as error #2 above. Question #2 triggers a Past-Condition → Present-Result mixed conditional — retrieval practice for error #1.

---

#### 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

**Tone & Bahasa:**
Encouraging, native-like, upper-intermediate tone. "Your mixed conditional is really solid here — this is the kind of structure that makes English sound natural when reflecting on life." "Just one small tense mismatch in the if-clause, and this would be flawless."

**Error Umum Topik Ini:**
1. Matching tenses incorrectly across clauses instead of mixing them deliberately
2. Using "would" instead of "would have" (or vice versa) depending on which clause refers to the past
3. Forgetting Past Perfect ("had + V3") in the if-clause for Past-Condition → Present-Result mixed conditionals
4. Confusing "hindsight" and "foresight"

**Template Pujian (Akhir Sesi):**
"Great work, [PANGGILAN] [NAMA]! Your mixed conditionals are starting to sound genuinely natural — this is one of the clearest signs of B2-level fluency. You're now able to connect a past decision to its present-day impact in a single sentence, which is exactly how native speakers reflect on life. Keep going!"

**Saran Naik Level (B2 → C1):**
"For C1, try combining mixed conditionals with inversion for emphasis ('Had I taken that job, I would now be living a very different life') and practice varying your hedging language ('arguably', 'in all likelihood') instead of stating things as plain facts."

---

#### 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

**Skenario Speaking:**
The user is having a thoughtful, slightly reflective conversation with Kak Ara about life decisions — like catching up with a mentor who asks genuinely curious "what if" questions about your past choices.

**Pertanyaan Lanjutan (jika user lancar):**
1. If you could give your younger self one piece of advice about a decision you made, what would it be?
2. Do you think you would have made the same decision if your circumstances had been different?

**Pattern Drill (jika user macet):**
Drill the mixed conditional pattern: "If I had + V3, I would + V1 (now)." / "If I + V2, I would have + V3 (then)."
- If I had + V3 ___, I would + V1 ___. → If I had taken that scholarship, I would be living abroad now.
- If I + V2 ___, I would have + V3 ___. → If I were more confident, I would have spoken up back then.

---

### DAY 2 — Getting Things Done: Services & Delegation

#### 📚 Detail Materi

**Target Kosakata (Box of Words):**

| No | Kosakata + Phonetic UK | English Definition | Catatan Indonesia |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | arrange /əˈreɪndʒ/ | to plan or organize something in advance | – |
| 2 | outsource /ˈaʊtsɔːs/ | to pay another company or person to do a task instead of doing it yourself | – |
| 3 | delegate /ˈdelɪɡeɪt/ | to give part of your work or authority to someone else | – |
| 4 | tailor (verb) /ˈteɪlər/ | to make or adjust something to suit a particular purpose | Hati-hati: ini verb (membuat/menyesuaikan sesuatu agar pas), bukan "tailor" sebagai kata benda (tukang jahit) |
| 5 | renovate /ˈrenəveɪt/ | to repair and improve a building so it's in good condition again | – |
| 6 | install /ɪnˈstɔːl/ | to put a piece of equipment or software in place, ready to be used | – |
| 7 | repair /rɪˈpeər/ | to fix something that is damaged or broken | – |
| 8 | inspect /ɪnˈspekt/ | to look at something closely to check its condition or quality | – |
| 9 | maintenance /ˈmeɪntənəns/ | the work needed to keep something in good condition | – |
| 10 | convenient /kənˈviːniənt/ | suitable for your needs, causing little trouble or effort | – |
| 11 | worthwhile /ˌwɜːθˈwaɪl/ | useful or important enough to be worth the time, money, or effort | – |
| 12 | get around to (phrasal verb) /ˈɡet əˈraʊnd tuː/ | to finally find time to do something after a delay | Frasa ini sering hilang konteksnya kalau diterjemahkan literal — artinya bukan "berkeliling ke", tapi "akhirnya sempat melakukan (setelah ditunda)" |
| 13 | take care of (fixed expression) /teɪk keər ɒv/ | to deal with or handle something/someone responsibly | – |
| 14 | hire /ˈhaɪər/ | to pay someone to do a job or service for you | – |
| 15 | professional (noun) /prəˈfeʃənl/ | a person with the skill or qualification to do a particular job | – |

**Grammar Pendukung (B2):**
- **Causative Verbs**: a structure used when someone arranges for another person to do something for them, instead of doing it themselves.
  - **have + object + V3 (past participle)**: subject *arranges* for the action to happen → "I **had my car repaired**." (someone else repaired it, on my request/arrangement)
  - **get + object + V3 (past participle)**: same meaning as "have", slightly more informal, often implies more effort to arrange → "I **got my house renovated**." (I made the arrangement happen)
  - **have/get + someone + V1 (bare infinitive)**: used when naming who performs the action → "I **had the technician install** the software." / "I **got my friend to help** me move."
- **Contrast with Passive Voice (the structure B2 learners most often confuse this with):** Passive voice ("My car **was repaired**") simply states that an action happened to something, without focus on *who arranged it*. Causative voice ("I **had my car repaired**") specifically emphasizes that the subject *arranged* for someone else to perform the action — there's a clear sense of delegation or instruction behind it. If the sentence implies "I paid/asked someone to do this for me," it's causative, not just passive.
- **Quick test:** ask "Did the subject arrange for this, or is it just describing what happened?" → If there's an implied arrangement/request, use causative (have/get + object + V3).

**Konteks Penggunaan:**
These words and structures describe getting tasks done by delegating them to other people or services — a very common real-life B2 topic (hiring contractors, IT support, professional services). Causative verbs are a clear B1→B2 marker: at B1, learners can only describe actions directly ("I repaired my car" or "My car was repaired"). At B2, learners can express the more nuanced idea of *arranging* for someone else to do something on their behalf — which is how adults actually talk about getting things done in daily and professional life.

---

#### ✅ Detail Task

**📖 Mode Cerita:**
Connected sentences describing a situation where you delegated tasks to others to get something done.
Example (using "outsource"): "Our company decided to outsource its customer service last year. We had a specialized agency handle all the calls, and honestly, it was worthwhile — response times improved a lot."
Write 7–9 sentences about a time you hired, delegated, or arranged for someone else to do something for you — it could be home renovation, a repair, a service at work, or even something as simple as getting your hair done. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words.
1. ...
2. ...
3. ...
4. ...
5. ...
6. ...
7. ...
(add sentence 8 and 9 if you want)

**⚡ Mode Kilat:**
Practice each word separately — 1 sentence per word, not connected as a story.
Example (same word "outsource"): "outsource: Many startups outsource their accounting to save time and focus on growth."
Choose 5 words from the Box of Words and write 1 causative-structure sentence for each:
- delegate: ...
- inspect: ...
- get around to: ...
- tailor: ...
- maintenance: ...

**Speaking Challenge (3 Pertanyaan):**
1. **Is there a task or chore you keep putting off and never get around to doing yourself? Would you consider hiring someone to take care of it?**
2. **Think of the last time you had something repaired or installed by a professional — was the result worth the cost?**
3. **If you ran your own business, which tasks would you delegate first, and which ones would you insist on doing yourself?**

---

#### 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi (8 Langkah)

**Langkah 1 — Koreksi Writing:**
Common errors among Indonesian learners with Causative Verbs (top 2 patterns get a deep "Why" explanation):
1. Using the active form instead of causative when delegation is implied: "I repaired my car" (when someone else actually did it) → "I **had my car repaired**." — *Why: in English, "I repaired my car" means YOU personally fixed it. If a mechanic did it because you arranged/paid for it, you must use the causative structure "have/get + object + V3" to show that you delegated the action. Catatan: Bahasa Indonesia sering pakai kalimat aktif untuk kedua situasi ini ("saya benerin mobil saya" bisa berarti benerin sendiri ATAU minta orang lain benerin) — English membedakan ini secara struktural, jadi penting untuk selalu cek: siapa yang BENERAN melakukan tindakannya?*
2. Using the wrong verb form after object in causative structure: "I had my car repair" or "I had my car repairing" → "I **had my car repaired**." — *Why: the structure is "have/get + object + V3 (past participle)", not V1 or V-ing. The object (my car) receives the action, so the verb form must be passive in meaning — V3, just like in passive voice ("my car was repaired").*
3. Confusing "have someone do something" with "have something done": "I had the technician installed the software" → "I **had the technician install** the software." — when you name the *person* doing the action right after have/get, use the bare infinitive (V1): "have + person + V1." When you name the *thing* being acted upon, use V3: "have + object + V3."

**Langkah 2 — Analisa BOW:**
Words that are often misused:
- **outsource** vs **delegate**: "outsource" = giving work to an external company/contractor ("We **outsource** our IT support to a third-party agency"), "delegate" = giving part of your own task/authority to someone within your team or close circle ("She **delegated** the report to her assistant"). Outsource = external, delegate = often internal.
- **tailor** (verb): always used with "to" when specifying purpose — "This service can be **tailored to** your specific needs." Don't confuse with the noun "tailor" (a person who makes clothes).
- **get around to**: always followed by a gerund (V-ing), never a bare infinitive — "I finally **got around to** fixing the leak." (✅) not "got around to fix" (❌).
- **worthwhile**: typically followed by a gerund or noun, not a full clause — "It was **worthwhile** hiring a professional." (✅)

**Langkah 3 — Analisa CEFR:**
Template: "Nice work, this is genuinely B2-level writing! Your causative structure is coming through — that's a clear step up from B1's simple active/passive descriptions. To push toward C1, try: (1) combining causative with passive-with-modal for more nuance ('This should have been installed by a professional, but I ended up getting it done myself'), (2) using more varied reporting structures when describing what a service provider told you ('The technician insisted on replacing the whole unit')."

**Langkah 4 — 5W+1H:**
Example table for the topic Services & Delegation:
| Elemen | Versi User | Versi Lebih Lengkap |
|---|---|---|
| What | I had my kitchen renovated | I finally had my entire kitchen renovated after putting it off for years |
| When | last month | last month, right before the holidays |
| Where | (not mentioned) | at my apartment, which hadn't been touched since I moved in |
| Why | (not mentioned) | because the old cabinets were falling apart and no longer worth repairing |
| Who | I | I, working with a local contractor I found through a friend |
| How | (not mentioned) | by hiring a small team instead of a big renovation company, which turned out to be more convenient and affordable |

**Enriched Paragraph:**
"I finally got around to renovating my kitchen last month. Instead of doing it myself, I had a local contractor handle the whole project — it was more convenient and, in the end, completely worthwhile. I also had the old wiring inspected, just to be safe."

**Langkah 5 — Transition Words:**
Best-fitting connectors for discussing services and delegation (B2 level):
- **instead of** → "Instead of fixing it myself, I had a professional take care of it."
- **as a result** → "I outsourced the task; as a result, I saved a lot of time."
- **on top of that** → "The service was fast, and on top of that, it was surprisingly affordable."

**Langkah 6 — Lexical Chunks & Collocation Check:**
Natural collocations B2+ speakers use for Services & Delegation: "get something done", "hand over (responsibility)", "take care of (a task)", "hire someone to do". Cek apakah tulisan user menggunakan collocation natural atau terdengar seperti terjemahan kata-per-kata dari Bahasa Indonesia. Sarankan 1 chunk kalau belum muncul.

**Langkah 7 — Register/Formality Check:**
Identify 1-2 phrases where the register doesn't match the topic's context (too casual for a professional/service context, or overly academic for everyday conversation about tasks). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (English, 1 sentence). ✅ skip if register is consistent throughout.

**Langkah 8 — Speaking Challenge:**
Question #1 ("never get around to doing yourself") directly recycles the "get around to" phrasal verb from the BOW. Question #2 ("had something repaired or installed") directly triggers the causative structure — the same pattern as error #1 above.

---

#### 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

**Tone & Bahasa:**
Encouraging, native-like, upper-intermediate tone. "Your causative structure is really clean here — you're clearly showing who arranged what, which is exactly the nuance B2 writing needs." "Just double-check the verb form after the object, and this is spot on."

**Error Umum Topik Ini:**
1. Using active voice instead of causative when delegation/arrangement is implied
2. Wrong verb form after the object (using V1/V-ing instead of V3 for "have/get + object + V3")
3. Confusing "have + person + V1" with "have + object + V3"
4. Confusing "outsource" (external) with "delegate" (often internal)

**Template Pujian (Akhir Sesi):**
"Great job, [PANGGILAN] [NAMA]! Your causative verbs are starting to sound really natural — you're clearly distinguishing between doing something yourself and arranging for someone else to do it, which is a genuinely B2-level skill. Keep practicing!"

**Saran Naik Level (B2 → C1):**
"For C1, try combining causative structures with passive-with-modal ('This should have been repaired sooner') and pay attention to more nuanced reporting verbs when quoting what a service provider or contractor told you ('She recommended replacing the entire system')."

---

#### 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

**Skenario Speaking:**
The user is chatting with Kak Ara about everyday tasks they've delegated or outsourced — like a casual conversation between friends comparing notes on which contractor or service to recommend.

**Pertanyaan Lanjutan (jika user lancar):**
1. Have you ever regretted hiring someone instead of doing a task yourself? What happened?
2. If money weren't an issue, what tasks would you outsource completely in your daily life?

**Pattern Drill (jika user macet):**
Drill the causative pattern: "I had/got + object + V3." / "I had/got + person + V1."
- I had/got + object + V3 ___. → I had my phone screen repaired.
- I had/got + person + V1 ___. → I got a friend to help me move the furniture.

### DAY 3 — Public Speaking & Memorable Impressions
**Grammar Focus:** Inversion with Negative Adverbials

#### 📚 Detail Materi

**Topik:** Public speaking, memorable impressions, dan momen-momen yang ngubah cara orang dipandang di depan umum — entah itu presentasi kerja, toast di pernikahan teman, atau pidato wisuda.

**Grammar Pendukung — Inversion with Negative Adverbials**

Day 3 memperkenalkan **Inversion**, struktur dimana auxiliary verb dipindah ke depan subject untuk efek emphasis — biasanya dipicu oleh negative adverbial di awal kalimat (Never, Rarely, Not only, Seldom, Under no circumstances).

Pola: **Negative Adverbial + Auxiliary + Subject + Main Verb**

- Never have I felt so nervous before walking on stage.
- Rarely do speakers get a standing ovation on their first attempt.
- Not only did she forget her notes, but she also froze for ten seconds.
- Under no circumstances should you read directly from your slides.

**Kontras dengan Day 2 (Causative Verbs):** Day 2 fokus ke siapa yang *melakukan* aksi vs siapa yang *menyuruh* orang lain melakukan aksi (have/get/make someone do something). Day 3 fokus ke *urutan kata* untuk emphasis — Inversion tidak mengubah siapa pelaku aksinya, tapi mengubah struktur kalimat supaya terdengar lebih formal dan dramatis. Error umum: user menambahkan auxiliary inversion TAPI lupa membalik urutan subject-verb di sisanya, atau memakai inversion dengan adverbial positif (salah — inversion ini khusus untuk negative/restrictive adverbial).

**Catatan:** Bahasa Indonesia tidak punya struktur inversion — urutan kata SPOK tetap sama walau ada kata "tidak pernah" di depan ("Tidak pernah saya merasa..."). Ini sering bikin user lupa membalik auxiliary-subject di English.

**Konteks Penggunaan:** Inversion banyak dipakai di speech formal, toast, opening keynote, atau saat user mau menyampaikan poin dengan bobot emosional lebih — bukan grammar buat percakapan santai sehari-hari.

#### ✅ Detail Task

**📦 Box of Words (BOW) — 15 kata:**

| Kosakata | English Definition | Catatan Indonesia |
|----------|---------------------|---------------------|
| podium /ˈpoʊdiəm/ | a raised platform a speaker stands on | — |
| stage fright /steɪdʒ fraɪt/ | nervousness before performing in public | — |
| captivate /ˈkæptɪveɪt/ | to hold someone's attention completely | — |
| rehearse /rɪˈhɜːrs/ | to practice a speech before delivering it | — |
| stumble (over words) /ˈstʌmbəl/ | to make a mistake while speaking | — |
| eloquent /ˈɛləkwənt/ | fluent and persuasive in speaking | — |
| anecdote /ˈænɪkdoʊt/ | a short personal story used to illustrate a point | — |
| resonate /ˈrɛzəneɪt/ | to have a meaningful emotional effect on listeners | — |
| composure /kəmˈpoʊʒər/ | calmness under pressure | — |
| memorable /ˈmɛmərəbəl/ | easy to remember because it stands out | — |
| come across (as) /kʌm əˈkrɒs/ | to give a particular impression | Bukan "datang melintasi" — di sini artinya "terkesan/terlihat sebagai" |
| freeze up /friːz ʌp/ | to suddenly be unable to speak or move from nervousness | — |
| win over /wɪn ˈoʊvər/ | to gain someone's support or approval | — |
| standing ovation /ˈstændɪŋ oʊˈveɪʃən/ | when an audience stands up and claps enthusiastically | — |
| profound /prəˈfaʊnd/ | very deep or intense in effect or meaning | — |

#### 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi (8 Langkah)

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli → Kalimat Benar → **Why** (English). "Catatan:" Indonesia HANYA untuk maks 1-2 pola error yang murni interferensi Bahasa Indonesia (contoh: lupa membalik auxiliary-subject setelah negative adverbial karena di Bahasa Indonesia urutan kata tidak berubah).

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — ✅/⚠️ per kata + contoh natural English. 🔂 **Vocab Refresh** — selipkan 1-2 kata dari Day 2 (arrange, outsource, delegate, tailor, renovate, install, repair, inspect, maintenance, convenient, worthwhile, get around to, take care of, hire, professional) di contoh kalimat baru.

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Level saat ini + tips konkret naik ke C1, terutama soal kapan inversion terdengar natural vs overused.

4️⃣ **Perbandingan 5W+1H** — Tabel What/Why/Where/When/Who/How (English). Di bawahnya "Enriched Paragraph" — full English, TANPA translation default.

5️⃣ **Transition Words** — Rekomendasikan 2-3 dari: notwithstanding, albeit, given that, provided that, by and large, all things considered + contoh English yang relevan ke konteks public speaking.

6️⃣ **Lexical Chunks & Collocation Check** — 2-3 natural collocations: "captivate the audience", "win over the crowd", "come across as confident". Cek apakah tulisan user pakai collocation natural atau terjemahan kata-per-kata dari Bahasa Indonesia. Sarankan 1 chunk kalau belum terdeteksi.
7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Identify 1-2 phrases where the register doesn't match the topic's context (too casual for formal topics, or overly academic/stiff for conversational ones). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (English, 1 sentence). ✅ skip if register is consistent throughout.
8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — 3 pertanyaan dalam English, tanpa translation default. Minimal 1 pertanyaan memicu retrieval inversion (contoh: "Describe a time you almost froze up on stage. Start your answer with 'Never have I...'").

#### 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

Kak Ara memberi encouragement dengan tone humble — apresiasi keberanian user mencoba struktur inversion yang memang termasuk salah satu yang paling sulit dikuasai di level B2, tanpa menggurui. Soroti progress dibanding Day 1-2 kalau terlihat.

#### 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

User mempraktikkan kalimat inversion secara lisan, dipicu oleh trigger eksplisit dari Kak Ara ("Coba ucapkan dengan struktur Never have I..."). Fokus ke intonasi emphasis yang biasanya menyertai inversion dalam speech natural.

#### 🔗 PROMPT — Day 3 (Copy-Paste ke ChatGPT)

```
Topik: Public Speaking & Memorable Impressions
Panggil aku [SAPAAN] [PANGGILAN].
Level bahasa Inggrisku: B2 (Upper-Intermediate).
Kamu Kak Ara dari Inggrisin Yuk, AI Coach. Bimbing aku vocab writing+speaking Level B2.
Gaya: sopan, ramah, humble - tunjukkan lewat ngobrol, jangan sebut diri seru/asyik.
Bahasa: English dominan. "Catatan:" Indonesia max 1-2 poin interferensi. Emoji ok. Phonetic UK dalam / /.
LANGKAH 1 - SAPAAN+BOW+WRITING CHALLENGE (1 response):
Sapa English, tampilkan BOW+Writing Challenge. Jangan tanya "ready?".
BOW (PERSIS 15 kata ini, jangan ganti):
podium, stage fright, captivate, rehearse, stumble (over words), eloquent, anecdote, resonate, composure, memorable, come across (as), freeze up, win over, standing ovation, profound
Tabel 3 kolom: Kosakata+phonetic UK | English definition | Catatan Indonesia ("-" default).
Writing Challenge (2 mode):
Mode Cerita: Write 7-9 sentences about a memorable public speaking experience (yours or someone you've seen). Min 5 kata dari BOW. Gunakan Inversion (Never have I..., Not only...but also...).
Mode Kilat: Pilih 5 kata dari BOW, 1 kalimat per kata.
(a) deskripsi singkat (b) contoh pakai KATA SAMA dari BOW (c) template latihan kosong.
Jangan bocorkan langkah koreksi - tunggu jawabanku.
LANGKAH 2 - KOREKSI 8 LANGKAH (otomatis setelah aku kirim tulisan):
1. Koreksi Writing - tabel 3 kolom: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat Benar | Why (English). Max 2 error utama. >=95% benar: OK. "Catatan:" max 1-2.
2. Analisa BOW - tiap kata: tepat/belum tepat + contoh English. Vocab Refresh: singgung 1-2 kata BOW Day sebelumnya.
3. Analisa CEFR - level saat ini + yang sudah bagus + 2 tips naik ke C1 (English).
4. 5W+1H - tabel English + "Enriched Paragraph": full English, no translation.
5. Transition Words - jika belum: 2-3 B2 connector (notwithstanding, albeit, given that, by and large) + contoh English.
6. Lexical Chunks - 2-3 collocations B2+ speakers use for topik ini. Format: chunk -> "example." (note). Sarankan 1 jika belum.
Kalau tulisanku kosong/off-topic/Indonesia: minta tulis 7-9 kalimat English dulu.
7. Register Check - 1-2 frasa register tidak cocok? Original -> Better -> Why (1 sentence English). OK jika konsisten.
8. Speaking Challenge - 3 pertanyaan English topik Public Speaking & Memorable Impressions (min 1 memicu retrieval grammar):
Have you ever had to speak in front of an audience - what helped you keep your composure?
Not only does delivery matter, but the message must resonate - what makes a speech truly memorable?
Think of a speaker who captivated you. What made them come across as so eloquent and profound?
LANGKAH 3 - MODE SPEAKING (trigger: Let's start speaking!):
Ulangi Speaking Challenge satu per satu, English. Langsung, jangan basa-basi.
Transkrip jawabanku ke Inggris. Koreksi dalam English. Kalau stuck: boleh 1 clue Indonesia singkat.
Feedback: kalimat lebih baik (B2) + penjelasan singkat English. Error B2 grammar -> bentuk benar dalam kurung italic.
"clue" -> petunjuk grammar saja. Lancar -> tambah 1 pertanyaan. Macet -> contoh + pattern drill.
Pujian singkat hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan tidak berlebihan.
```

### DAY 4 — Scientific Research & Academic Publishing
**Grammar Focus:** Passive Voice with Modals

#### 📚 Detail Materi

**Topik:** Scientific research, academic publishing, peer review, dan cara ilmuwan mengomunikasikan temuan mereka secara objektif.

**Grammar Pendukung — Passive Voice with Modals**

Day 4 menggabungkan Passive Voice dengan modal verbs (can, must, should, may, could) — struktur yang sangat umum di academic writing untuk menjaga objektivitas (fokus ke aksi/hasil, bukan ke pelaku).

Pola: **Subject + Modal + be + Past Participle**

- The results can be replicated under controlled conditions.
- This hypothesis must be tested before publication.
- The data should be reviewed by an independent panel.
- Further research may be required to confirm these findings.

**Kontras dengan Day 3 (Inversion):** Day 3 fokus ke urutan kata untuk emphasis dramatis di speech. Day 4 fokus ke menghilangkan fokus pada pelaku aksi (siapa yang melakukan) supaya tulisan terdengar objektif dan formal — khas gaya akademik. Error umum: user lupa menambahkan "be" setelah modal (salah: "must tested", benar: "must be tested"), atau memakai active voice padahal konteksnya menuntut objektivitas akademik.

**Catatan:** Di Bahasa Indonesia, passive voice sering ditandai dengan "di-" (diuji, ditinjau) tapi modal+passive ("harus diuji") kadang diterjemahkan langsung jadi "must tested" tanpa "be" — ini error interferensi yang umum.

**Konteks Penggunaan:** Passive + modal dipakai di abstrak jurnal, laporan riset, proposal penelitian — situasi formal dimana proses/hasil lebih penting daripada siapa pelakunya.

#### ✅ Detail Task

**📦 Box of Words (BOW) — 15 kata:**

| Kosakata | English Definition | Catatan Indonesia |
|----------|---------------------|---------------------|
| hypothesis /haɪˈpɒθəsɪs/ | a proposed explanation to be tested | — |
| methodology /ˌmɛθəˈdɒlədʒi/ | the system of methods used in research | — |
| peer review /pɪr rɪˈvjuː/ | evaluation of work by experts in the same field | — |
| replicate /ˈrɛplɪkeɪt/ | to repeat a study to verify its results | — |
| empirical /ɛmˈpɪrɪkəl/ | based on observation or experiment, not theory alone | — |
| variable /ˈvɛriəbəl/ | a factor that can change in an experiment | — |
| significant /sɪɡˈnɪfɪkənt/ | (statistically) meaningful, not due to chance | Bukan "penting" secara umum, tapi makna statistik khusus |
| findings /ˈfaɪndɪŋz/ | the results or conclusions of a study | — |
| publication /ˌpʌblɪˈkeɪʃən/ | the act of making research publicly available | — |
| bias /ˈbaɪəs/ | a systematic distortion affecting results unfairly | — |
| draw a conclusion /drɔː ə kənˈkluːʒən/ | to form a final judgment based on evidence | — |
| rule out /ruːl aʊt/ | to eliminate something as a possibility | — |
| carry out (research) /ˈkæri aʊt/ | to perform or conduct something | — |
| validate /ˈvælɪdeɪt/ | to confirm that something is accurate or sound | — |
| inconclusive /ˌɪnkənˈkluːsɪv/ | not leading to a definite result | — |

#### 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi (8 Langkah)

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli → Kalimat Benar → **Why** (English). "Catatan:" Indonesia HANYA untuk maks 1-2 pola error interferensi Bahasa Indonesia (contoh: lupa "be" setelah modal dalam passive).

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — ✅/⚠️ per kata + contoh natural English. 🔂 **Vocab Refresh** — selipkan 1-2 kata dari Day 3 (podium, stage fright, captivate, rehearse, stumble, eloquent, anecdote, resonate, composure, memorable, come across as, freeze up, win over, standing ovation, profound) di contoh kalimat baru.

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Level saat ini + tips konkret naik ke C1, terutama soal nuance penggunaan modal (must vs should vs may) dalam academic hedging.

4️⃣ **Perbandingan 5W+1H** — Tabel What/Why/Where/When/Who/How (English). Di bawahnya "Enriched Paragraph" — full English, TANPA translation default.

5️⃣ **Transition Words** — Rekomendasikan 2-3 dari: notwithstanding, albeit, given that, provided that, by and large, all things considered + contoh English relevan ke konteks academic research.

6️⃣ **Lexical Chunks & Collocation Check** — 2-3 natural collocations: "carry out research", "draw a conclusion", "rule out other factors". Cek apakah tulisan user pakai collocation natural atau terjemahan kata-per-kata. Sarankan 1 chunk kalau belum terdeteksi.
7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Identify 1-2 phrases where the register doesn't match the topic's context (too casual for formal topics, or overly academic/stiff for conversational ones). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (English, 1 sentence). ✅ skip if register is consistent throughout.
8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — 3 pertanyaan dalam English, tanpa translation default. Minimal 1 pertanyaan memicu retrieval passive+modal (contoh: "What do you think should be done before any research is published?").

#### 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

Kak Ara mengapresiasi usaha user menulis dengan gaya akademik yang lebih formal dari biasanya — tone humble, akui bahwa passive+modal memang salah satu struktur yang terasa kaku di awal tapi penting buat konteks formal/akademik.

#### 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

User mempraktikkan kalimat passive+modal secara lisan, dipicu trigger eksplisit dari Kak Ara. Fokus ke pelafalan modal+be (should be, must be, can be) yang sering diucapkan terpisah-pisah oleh pemula.
